## Instruction

Please help me check which products are in my shop, filter out those that have been in stock for more than 90 days and have sold fewer than 10 units in the past 30 days. Move them to a product category named "Outlet/Clearance" ("/" is part of the name). Also, send an email to each of the subscribed customers.

You can find the email template under the workspace (please sort the products by stock-in time from earliest to latest; if the stock-in time is the same, then sort by discount ratio from small to large). The subscriber information is in subscriber.json.

## Initial State

### Local Workspace

<div className="file-tree">

├── blog_template.md
├── email_template.txt
└── subscriber.json
</div>

### WooCommerce

The data is reinitialized on each test; you can review the original data construction process [here](https://github.com/hkust-nlp/mcpbench_dev/blob/finalpool_dev/tasks/finalpool/filter-low-selling-products/preprocess).

```python
import json, datetime, re
from dateutil import parser
p = '/workspace/dumps/workspace/.overlong_tool_outputs/UKBZZYVM6DQ2WJ53c5td72.json'
with open(p,'r',encoding='utf-8') as f:
    data = json.load(f)
text = data['text']
products = json.loads(text)
# helper to get meta value

def get_meta(prod, key):
    for m in prod.get('meta_data', []):
        if m.get('key') == key:
            v = m.get('value')
            try:
                return int(v)
            except Exception:
                try:
                    return float(v)
                except Exception:
                    return v
    return None

# date threshold
now = datetime.datetime(2025,10,16)
threshold = now - datetime.timedelta(days=90)

selected = []
for prod in products:
    dc = parser.parse(prod['date_created'])
    sales30 = get_meta(prod, 'sales_last_30_days')
    if dc <= threshold and sales30 is not None and sales30 < 10 and prod.get('stock_status') == 'instock':
        reg = float(prod.get('regular_price') or 0)
        sale = prod.get('sale_price')
        price = float((sale if sale else prod.get('price') or 0))
        ratio = price / reg if reg else 1.0
        selected.append({
            'id': prod['id'],
            'name': prod['name'],
            'date_created': dc,
            'sales_last_30_days': sales30,
            'regular_price': reg,
            'price': price,
            'sale_price': float(sale) if sale else None,
            'discount_ratio': ratio
        })

selected_sorted = sorted(selected, key=lambda x: (x['date_created'], x['discount_ratio']))
print('COUNT', len(selected_sorted))
for s in selected_sorted[:20]:
    print(s['id'], s['name'], s['date_created'].date(), s['sales_last_30_days'], s['regular_price'], s['price'], s['discount_ratio'])
 code
```

```python
import json, sys
p = '/workspace/dumps/workspace/.overlong_tool_outputs/UKBZZYVM6DQ2WJ53c5td72.json'
with open(p,'r',encoding='utf-8') as f:
    outer = json.load(f)
text = outer.get('text')
layer = 0
while True:
    if isinstance(text, str) and text.strip().startswith('{'):
        obj = json.loads(text)
        if isinstance(obj, dict) and 'text' in obj:
            text = obj['text']
            layer += 1
            continue
        else:
            break
    elif isinstance(text, str) and text.strip().startswith('['):
        products = json.loads(text)
        break
    else:
        # already parsed
        products = text
        break
print('layers:', layer)
print(type(products))
if isinstance(products, list):
    print('count', len(products))
    print('first keys', products[0].keys())
else:
    print('not list', type(products))
    print(str(products)[:200])
 code
```
